Trump deal with Iran, gas prices, economics & more addressed during Scott Bessent, Larry Kudlow chat

USA TODAY(7.5M) ·28:12 ·24.8K views · 2026-05-29
Scott Bessent (U.S. Treasury Secretary) Larry Kudlow (Host, Fox Business)
Treasury Secretary Scott Bessent outlines how the administration's "Operation Economic Fury" and naval blockade have financially crippled Iran, forcing them to negotiate on nuclear enrichment, while domestic supply-side economic reforms and the newly launched Trump Savings Accounts continue to drive historic U.S.
TL;DR Treasury Secretary Scott Bessent outlines how the administration's "Operation Economic Fury" and naval blockade have financially crippled Iran, forcing them to negotiate on nuclear enrichment, while domestic supply-side economic reforms and the newly launched Trump...

TL;DR

Treasury Secretary Scott Bessent outlines how the administration's "Operation Economic Fury" and naval blockade have financially crippled Iran, forcing them to negotiate on nuclear enrichment, while domestic supply-side economic reforms and the newly launched Trump Savings Accounts continue to drive historic U.S. business investment and consumer resilience.

***

The Economic Blockade and Negotiations with Iran

  • Economic Stragulation: Through "Operation Economic Fury," the Treasury Department and the U.S. Navy have successfully shut down Iran’s financial pipelines, leaving the nation at the end of its financial tether.
      • Internal Collapse: Iran is experiencing over 200% inflation, is distributing food vouchers, has cut off internet access, and is failing to pay 40% to 50% of its military and police forces.
      • Decapitated Leadership: Diplomatic efforts are dealing with "third-level" officials, as the first two tiers of leadership have been decapitated. Negotiations are complicated by navigating both a cleric-led theocracy and an IRGC-led "thugocracy."
  • Naval Blockade and Oil Shutoff: The U.S. Navy has successfully blockaded Iranian ports, including Kharg Island, Iran's primary oil export facility, completely shutting it down. Iran's only remaining oil client is China, and their volume of oil on the water is at its lowest historical levels.
  • Seizure of Assets:
      • Crypto and Offshore Accounts: Treasury has directly seized approximately $1 billion in cryptocurrency wallets belonging to Iranian actors and is working with European allies to freeze luxury villas and properties.
      • IRGC Theft: Prior to the blockade, leaders of the Islamic Revolutionary Guard Corps (IRGC) were estimated to be stealing $400 million to $500 million per month, divided among roughly 80 leaders.
      • GCC Alignment: Following missile and drone attacks from Iran, GCC Gulf allies have closed banking loopholes and partnered with the U.S. to freeze illicit Iranian accounts.

U.S. Economic Boom and Supply-Side Success

  • Historic Business Investment: Despite temporary energy price spikes, non-defense capital goods and business investment have grown at an annualized rate of nearly 19% over the past three months (10.5% year-over-year).
      • Productivity & Unit Labor Costs: Productivity is up nearly 3%, while unit labor costs—a critical long-term inflation metric—sit at a low 1.2% over the last four quarters.
  • The "One Big Beautiful Bill": Bessent credited permanent tax cuts, full expensing, and the collaboration of House Speaker Mike Johnson, Jason Smith, French Hill, Jodey Arrington, and Leader John Thune for establishing permanent policy certainty for U.S. businesses.
  • Consumer Purchasing Power: While gasoline prices reached a temporary high of $4.50 before beginning to decline, the average household impact was limited to under $200 in extra fuel costs.
      • Grocery Price Correction: Wholesale food prices are stabilizing. While beef remains high due to cattle disease in Mexico, egg prices are down 90%, and chicken and vegetables are also down.

Trump Savings Accounts and the 250th American Anniversary

  • Trump Savings Accounts (TSAs): Hailed by Bessent as the most significant government benefit for young people since the GI Bill, TSAs aim to expand equity market exposure to the 38% of Americans who currently have none.
      • Funding Structure: Children born during the President's term will receive a $1,000 seed investment from the Treasury into low-cost index funds.
      • Family Contributions: Families can contribute up to $5,000 tax-free annually until the child reaches age 18. Funds can then be rolled into retirement plans, used for higher education, or utilized as a down payment on a home.
      • Philanthropic Support: Billionaire philanthropists Michael and Susan Dell have committed $6.25 billion directly to TSAs for children in the bottom 80% of economic zip codes. Additionally, 20 states have committed to topping up these accounts.
  • Proposed $250 Currency Note: In celebration of America's 250th anniversary, there is active legislative interest in issuing a $250 bill featuring President Trump, modeled after the Calvin Coolidge coin minted for the 150th anniversary.
      • Seigniorage Advantage: Bessent noted that printing a $250 bill acts as an interest-free loan to the government because citizens are highly likely to hold and collect the physical currency rather than spend it.

Monetary Policy and the "Warsh Fed"

  • A New Era at the Federal Reserve: Bessent expressed high confidence in newly confirmed Fed Chairman Kevin Warsh, predicting a return to institutional credibility, transparency, and simplicity.
      • Forward Guidance: Bessent confirmed 100% agreement with Chairman Warsh's objective to eliminate "forward guidance" in favor of returning to standard Fed accountability.
  • Fed Independence: Bessent reiterated that President Trump intends to let the Fed Chairman operate independently without political pressure regarding interest rate adjustments.
  • Strong Dollar Policy: Bessent, a 35-year currency market veteran, affirmed that the administration remains fully committed to maintaining the U.S. dollar as the global reserve currency, defined by maintaining reliable, long-term real returns for global investors.

***

Gemini co-leads on project origins and what's next

Google for Developers(2.6M) ·42:00 ·7.3K views · 2026-05-29
Logan Kilpatrick (Host & AI Advocate, Google) Jeff Dean (Chief Scientist, Google) Noam Shazeer (Co-lead of Gemini, Google)
The Gemini project was established by consolidating Google's fragmented AI research teams and compute resources into a unified effort.
TL;DR The Gemini project was established by consolidating Google's fragmented AI research teams and compute resources into a unified effort. This strategic alignment has accelerated multimodal "world modeling," yielded highly efficient model distillation (packing "Pro"...

TL;DR

The Gemini project was established by consolidating Google's fragmented AI research teams and compute resources into a unified effort. This strategic alignment has accelerated multimodal "world modeling," yielded highly efficient model distillation (packing "Pro" capabilities into "Flash" versions), and set the stage for agentic self-learning systems.

The Origins and Consolidation of Project Gemini

  • Eliminating Fragmentation: Prior to Gemini, Google's AI efforts were split across DeepMind and Google Brain (working on Pathways, PaLM, and PaLM 2). Jeff Dean authored a half-page memo arguing that splitting compute and talent was "silly" and that Google must consolidate into a single, unified team to build a frontier model.
  • The "Gemini" Name: The project's name stems from "twins," representing the map-and-reduce fusion of Google’s two premier AI research groups (and nod to Jeff Dean having twins).
  • Deep Collaborative Roots: The leadership team shares decades of history:
      • Jeff Dean recruited Noam Shazeer to Google in 2000 and acted as his engineering mentor.
      • Dean recruited Oriol Vinyals in 2012 to the Google Brain team to work on early deep learning models and distillation.
      • Dean and Koray Kavukcuoglu first collaborated by reviewing raw codebase directories together during Google's acquisition of DeepMind.

Model Performance, Distillation, and the "Flash" Phenomenon

  • The Generation Leap: A consistent, positive surprise for the team is that each subsequent "Flash" generation successfully packs the intelligence of the previous generation’s larger "Pro" model, accelerating efficiency.
  • The Distillation Recipe: Rather than using complex ensembles of dozens of models, Google uses a highly optimized student-teacher distillation process with modest tweaks to the original distillation paper.
  • Multimodal Joint Training: By training jointly across text, video, audio, and physical world datasets (such as robotics, lidar, and genomics), the model develops "world modeling" capabilities—understanding and simulating visual consistency, depth, and physical dynamics.
  • The Evaluation Bottleneck: Robustly evaluating LLM capabilities in a way that aligns with real-world user experiences (rather than overfitting to leaked benchmarks) remains one of the most persistent and critical challenges in frontier AI development.

Predictions and Technical Frontiers for 2027

  • Self-Learning and Agentic Research: The team predicts that within a few years, models will use agentic workflows to actively research, run experiments, and improve subsequent generations of Gemini under human guidance.
  • Dynamic Continual Learning: Researchers are aiming for a paradigm shift where models dynamically update their internal knowledge bases through interaction and experience without needing expensive weight updates.
  • Tool Latency as a Bottleneck: As autonomous agents run for longer periods (e.g., executing tasks over 30 days), the primary bottleneck will be the latency of current digital tools, which were designed for human speed rather than model speed.
  • The Efficiency Gap: Humans require vastly less data to learn. A human hears roughly one billion words in a lifetime, whereas models require trillions of tokens to achieve similar capabilities. Closing this data-efficiency gap is a key algorithmic priority.

The Evolution of Google's Product Strategy

  • The "One Box" Realization: Modern general-purpose models fulfill Google’s early search philosophy of a single "one-box" interface, but with a unified backend instead of fragmented custom engines.
  • The Ecosystem Debate: The leadership team debated whether AI will eventually consolidate into a single central "model product" or diverge into thousands of specialized products:
      • Single Model View: Oriol Vinyals noted that there is clearly one unified model powering the backend, though users may still prefer distinct digital interfaces for separation of concerns.
      • Multitude of Products: Koray Kavukcuoglu expects a massive expansion of niche products because general intelligence will make it incredibly cheap and easy to build specialized applications.

Notable Quotes

"This is silly. We are fragmenting our efforts and fragmenting our compute. And if we're going to build an incredibly powerful model, we need to all come together and work on building a single model." — Jeff Dean
"It's like squeezing the lemon. You squeeze the lemon, the juice comes out, it's the good bits, you put it in a glass which is your small model." — Koray Kavukcuoglu
"The user would assume, 'Oh, there must be some brilliant general-purpose AI behind the whole thing...' and now we actually built it. We built the general-purpose AI. It is one box." — Noam Shazeer
"I really didn't expect we could keep doing what we've been doing generation after generation, which is to pack the intelligence of Pro back into Flash." — Oriol Vinyals

I think, you know, that was actually pretty obvious that if you have a model that is used by a lot of people, you're going to get a lot of lessons and experience of what's working well and what's not working well. And, you know, we've seen this in Search for many, many years. The use of Search by our users really informs, you know, what are the things it's not doing well, what are the things we should be doing better, you know, aggregating lots of interesting usage statistics to understand that in a deeper way, and then working on improving those things is important. AI models should be no different, right? It seemed like that was pretty obvious from the beginning, but we had to have a thing out there that people were using. Yeah, that's the true test. Like, people using it, and is it useful... useful to people? Because if you go in a box and you try to hill-climb benchmarks, then you end up hill-climbing benchmarks and, you know, maybe you leaked your benchmark. It... it doesn't end up well. You don't want to build intelligence in a black box. You want it to be useful. You want people to be using it. Therefore, understanding what is required, like what is scratching the frontier, is both scratching the frontier of the research in terms of technical capability, but also scratching the surface of what is the next thing that you can enable for users. You can't do it if you don't actually do it with the products, and those two hand-in-hand define what the frontier means. So at the time, like Gemini starts, there are already a lot of machine learning models making it into products. And I think what seemed obvious is that if we create a single model more powerful than the average of the other models, like powering everything, that had to be like a leap forward. Whether there was a single product that could be created around that single, you know, model, maybe wasn't as clear at the time. But I think it was very clear that putting all the compute and intelligence into a single powerful model was going to leapfrog many things Google was already using machine learning for. And that was very exciting to be given that amount of compute and responsibility initially, but I think it's proven to be, indeed, kind of the... the core engine of Google intelligence. Even before we started the Gemini effort, there were a lot of people thinking about, you know, building incredibly general-purpose models that could do things. At some point, research in AI was a lot more academic, right? Like, you go back 10 years, it was a lot more academic research. And at that point, how you organize it is not really the key element. It is more about the exploration, and the speed of exploration is important. But as things get more and more focused, what you want is to really, as Jeff pointed out, have this focused operation. Rather than us trying to build things in parallel, because these things require a lot more focus and effort—and each one of them is like a major operation in terms of many researchers coming together and solving many problems—at that point, I think it was really, really a good idea to say, "Okay, this is the moment that we need to change." He had some good ideas about how to get a bigger model to transfer into a smaller model, and I was like, "We've got to show this thing at scale." So we trained a 50-model ensemble for 300 million images, which was a lot at that time. They were 50 distinct ones, so we grouped the categories—like this one was going to be good at cars, and this one was going to be good at wild animals. Then we transferred the knowledge with distillation into a single model, and it was much more accurate than the single model you could have trained on the raw data. This is not an "Interview Logan" episode, but... Maybe we should have some of those. No, you don't want to hear what I have to say. The model is the product, that's all I have to say. I want the models to get better. No, I think the long-run stuff will be really interesting to see, because I feel like that's a frontier we can really easily track. Even if coding models get 20% better tomorrow and they're really good, I still think you'll run into limitations for how long you want the model to run autonomously. It feels like that's something where, at I/O 2027, if we're able to say, "This model's been running for 30 days" leading up to I/O, that would be really surprising to a lot of people. Maybe we won't say that, but it is something to shoot for. But that quantity of work being done independently by the model would be surprising. Exactly. And I think it actually takes the full stack to pull that off. You're going to need memory systems, you're going to need continual learning, and you're going to need better hardware, because it's going to cost a zillion tokens to let something run for 30 days. Well, and also you want your better hardware to have low latency, because if it finished in one day, you'd be way happier than waiting 30 days. 30 days is a good marketing line, but I'd actually be happy with one. Another prediction—well, not a prediction for announcements, but one thing that these agents are going to stress—is that all of our tools are too slow, right? So 29 and a half days of those 30 days are spent waiting, like, "list file," "read file," "check everything." Yeah, I mean, I think there are many product outlets, and there's a smaller number of things that make those products amazing. If you think about the glasses that were demonstrated at I/O, that's a product. But it's going to be made better because the models are better, they understand audio better, and they can speak to you better. That is a distinct product from Search. Exactly, right. I think it's clear to us there's definitely one model powering whatever it is. I'm not an expert, but as a user, sometimes I feel like I make an active choice of what I want to do with a digital device—like check my calendar, write an email, or buy something. Having that division might be more of a human factor rather than the technology being incapable of presenting all of this in a single product. JPMorgan Chase CEO Jamie Dimon speaks at Reagan National Economic Forum — 5/29/2026

CNBC Television(3.4M) ·39:22 ·15.9K views · 2026-05-29
Jamie Dimon (CEO, JPMorgan Chase) Morgan Brennan (Anchor, CNBC)
JPMorgan Chase CEO Jamie Dimon warns that shifting global geopolitics and domestic bureaucratic inertia are the greatest threats to Western democracy, urging the U.S.
TL;DR JPMorgan Chase CEO Jamie Dimon warns that shifting global geopolitics and domestic bureaucratic inertia are the greatest threats to Western democracy, urging the U.S. to deploy "smart industrial policy" to secure critical supply chains, enact aggressive regulatory reforms...

TL;DR

JPMorgan Chase CEO Jamie Dimon warns that shifting global geopolitics and domestic bureaucratic inertia are the greatest threats to Western democracy, urging the U.S. to deploy "smart industrial policy" to secure critical supply chains, enact aggressive regulatory reforms to spark GDP growth, and take a decisive stance against foreign adversaries.

Geopolitics, Alliances, and Dollar Dominance

  • Shifting Tectonic Plates: Dimon emphasizes that escalating geopolitical tensions—including the war in Ukraine, conflicts in the Middle East, and the actions of the "evil axis" (Russia, Iran, and North Korea)—completely dwarf short-term economic forecasts and threaten the future of the free world.
  • The Threat of Iran: Dimon advocates for a more aggressive foreign policy stance, stating that the U.S. should have taken decisive coalition action against Iran decades ago to prevent state-sponsored terrorism.
      • Nuclear Proliferation: He warns that if Iran successfully acquires nuclear weapons, it will trigger rapid nuclear proliferation across Egypt, Saudi Arabia, the UAE, Kuwait, South Korea, the Philippines, Japan, and Australia.
  • Economic Realpolitik and Dollar Dominance: The U.S. dollar's status as the global reserve currency is directly dependent on the U.S. maintaining both the preeminent military and the preeminent economy in the world.
  • Strengthening Western Alliances: Dimon suggests the Western world must deep-link its economic relationships to counter adversaries like China.
      • European Trade: He proposes that the U.S. should offer Europe a major free trade agreement conditional on structural economic reforms (referencing the Draghi report).
      • North American Integration: He urges a swift and favorable resolution to USMCA negotiations, highlighting that Canada and Mexico share a vital, common economic system with the U.S. that includes critical resources like oil, gas, lithium, and potash.

The $1.5T Security and Resiliency Initiative

  • Direct Capital Injection: Under Dimon's leadership, JPMorgan Chase launched a $1.5 trillion, 10-year Security and Resiliency Initiative to finance domestic and allied capabilities in critical sectors. The firm expects to exceed this $1.5 trillion target.
  • Strategic Focus Sectors: The initiative focuses on securing supply chains in key areas, including:
      • Military equipment, drones, and missiles.
      • Active pharmaceutical ingredients (APIs) and semiconductors.
      • Rare earth elements and advanced manufacturing.
      • Liquefied natural gas (LNG) infrastructure to support European allies.
  • Smart Industrial Policy: Dimon advocates for targeted government intervention to rebuild critical supply chains, rejecting the idea that this constitutes "state capitalism."
      • Rare Earths Example: The U.S. currently imports only $200 million in rare earth elements. Dimon argues that implementing high tariffs or unilateral import bans on Chinese rare earths would force domestic resiliency. While this might slightly raise costs (e.g., adding $100 to the price of a car), it would achieve 100% supply chain security.

Domestic Reform and Reigniting the "American Dream"

  • The Permitting Crisis: Dimon criticizes U.S. regulatory and permitting delays as a "disgrace," noting that infrastructure projects like rebuilding the Baltimore bridge are mired in bureaucracy.
      • "Free" Growth Policy: He challenges Congress to spend six months passing cost-free regulatory and permitting reforms (without debating revenues or expenses) to boost GDP growth by an estimated 1%.
  • Supporting the Bottom 30%: While the top 70% of Americans are thriving, the bottom 30% have experienced 25 years of wage stagnation. Dimon asserts that throwing federal money at the problem has failed, and solutions must focus on local policies regarding housing, crime, and education.
  • Tax Policy and Earned Income Tax Credit (EITC): Aligning with Jeff Bezos’s recent comments that the government has a spending problem rather than a revenue problem, Dimon champions the expansion of the EITC.
      • EITC Proposal: He recommends expanding the credit to single workers earning $12,000–$14,000 and removing the child requirement. This $50 billion expansion would encourage workforce entry, reduce crime and suicide rates, and pay for itself through improved social and economic outcomes.
  • JPMorgan's "American Dream Initiative": The bank is expanding branches in low-income neighborhoods, teaching financial literacy, and scaling its small business banking footprint with the goal of growing from 7 million to 10 million small business clients.

Monetary Policy, Inflation, and Market Risks

  • The Fed Under Kevin Warsh: Dimon welcomes newly appointed Federal Reserve Chair Kevin Warsh, praising his market experience and fresh perspective.
      • Regulatory Rollback: Dimon supports Warsh's intent to reduce the Fed’s balance sheet, scale back quantitative easing (QE), and steer the Fed away from non-monetary issues like climate change and DEI, allowing the OCC to handle primary bank regulation.
  • Structural Inflationary Forces: Dimon believes inflation is far stickier than the market assumes. Ongoing inflationary pressures include:
      • Global remilitarization and the restructuring of global trade.
      • Heavy spending on AI infrastructure.
      • Domestic immigration limits.
      • The cumulative effect of consecutive $2 trillion annual federal deficits.
  • Market Exuberance and Credit Cycle Concerns: Dimon views current equity and debt markets as highly exuberant, driven by AI hype. While JPMorgan is prepared for interest rates ranging from 2% to 8%, Dimon warns that low credit spreads present a real risk.
      • Private Credit: He does not view the $1.7 trillion private credit market as a systemic threat, but expects weak underwriting standards and a lack of transparency to result in worse-than-expected credit performance during the next downturn.

JPMorgan Strategy and M&A

  • Strategic Acquisitions: Dimon confirms JPMorgan is open to deploying its excess capital toward acquisitions in the $10 billion to $20 billion range to enhance its capabilities in payments, asset management, and capital raising.
  • Competitive Focus: Rather than focusing on its current market leadership, JPMorgan's management is focused on areas where competitors are winning, studying platforms like Citadel, Stripe, and Revolut to improve the bank's own systems and digital offerings.

Notable Quotes

"If you want to keep the dollar as the reserve currency... if we're not the preeminent military and the preeminent economy in the world in 30 years, we will not be the preeminent reserve currency. They actually go hand in hand." — Jamie Dimon
"Next time we should go for the head of the snake... Iran having a nuclear weapon may be the biggest threat facing mankind. Because if they have it, so will Egypt, Saudi Arabia, UAE, Kuwait, South Korea, Philippines, Japan, Australia, and then I don't know how you stop proliferation at that point." — Jamie Dimon
"Good policy is free. Take six months in Congress. Do not raise revenues or cut expenses... Just change policy. That makes things better. Housing policy, permitting policy, local affordable housing policy, education policy. I think it will drive growth 1% higher just by doing that." — Jamie Dimon
"I just want that gravestone to say, you know, when people visit, 'We're better off because of that son of a bitch.'" — Jamie Dimon

Builders Unscripted: Ep. 3 - Matias Castello, Product Leader at Alchemy

OpenAI(2.0M) ·29:50 ·1.3K views · 2026-05-29
Matias Castello (Product Lead at Alchemy) Romain Huet (Head of Developer Experience, OpenAI)
Matias Castello (Product Lead at Alchemy) leverages Codex and GPT-5.5 to automate the software development lifecycle, proving that non-engineers can build production-ready software by managing AI agents that autonomously research, draft plans, write code, and execute pull requests.
TL;DR Matias Castello (Product Lead at Alchemy) leverages Codex and GPT-5.5 to automate the software development lifecycle, proving that non-engineers can build production-ready software by managing AI agents that autonomously research, draft plans, write code, and execute...

TL;DR

Matias Castello (Product Lead at Alchemy) leverages Codex and GPT-5.5 to automate the software development lifecycle, proving that non-engineers can build production-ready software by managing AI agents that autonomously research, draft plans, write code, and execute pull requests.

Integrating AI at Alchemy: From Documentation to Peer Review

  • Initial Adoption: Directing edits to developer documentation.
    • Alchemy first integrated Codex directly into Slack to make small edits to developer docs. This allowed team members to bypass running the documentation site locally.
  • The Turning Point: Retroactive bug detection.
    • During a post-mortem for a migration incident, the team tested whether Codex could have detected the underlying race condition bug. Codex successfully caught it, accelerating internal trust in the model.
  • Collaborative Code Review: Integrating AI into the PR pipeline.
    • Software engineers at Alchemy now tag Codex directly within pull request comments to iteratively refine code before shipping.
    • Romain Huet noted that while companies like Datadog found 1 in 5 historical incidents could be prevented by AI reviews, newer models like GPT-5.5 could potentially catch upwards of 90% of code issues.

Paradigm Shift: Designing for the AI-Assisted Developer and Agent

  • Changing Target Audiences: Designing infrastructure for AI users.
    • As a developer platform, Alchemy now assumes that 100% of human developers build software with AI assistance, requiring a redesign of their onboarding and tooling patterns.
  • Autonomous Agents as Customers: Adapting platforms for machine users.
    • Matias highlights a growing segment of "agentic" developers—autonomous AI systems that register, integrate APIs, and execute transactions on the blockchain independently.
  • Shrinking MVP Timelines: The democratization of startup building.
    • Matias estimates that MVPs that previously took months and a dedicated team of engineers to build can now be shipped by a solo founder in less than a week.
    • Romain shared that his first startup required a team of 15 engineers and 18 months to reach a V1 release, a timeline that has been dramatically compressed by modern models.

Autonomous Side-Project Workflows: Leveraging Codex to Build Asynchronously

  • The "Codex Moment" Strategy: Running AI pipelines in parallel with life.
    • To maximize output without constant screen time, Matias schedules multi-hour Codex tasks during his lunch breaks, before going to sleep, or prior to leaving for social events.
  • Autonomous Project Management: Integrating AI with Linear.
    • Matias uses a custom setup where Codex acts as the project manager: it creates a plan, breaks it down into Linear milestones, generates over 150 tasks, and self-assigns and closes out the issues.
  • The `agents.md` Context File: Eliminating alignment drift.
    • To prevent AI agents from making incorrect assumptions, Matias initializes every repository with an `agents.md` file detailing his structural, stylistic, and technical coding preferences.
  • Competitor Research & Modular Feature Flags: Automated feature generation.
    • Matias tasks Codex with analyzing competitor features overnight. Codex scores the best ideas, writes the code, and deploys them into his app behind modular feature flags, allowing him to simply toggle them on or off to test the results the next morning.

Hands-On Testing: Wearables, Computer Use, and "Snapcat" Evals

  • Apple Watch and Voice Triggers: Coding on the go.
    • Matias built a custom Apple Watch complication and companion iPhone app using the Codex App Server. This allows him to dictate a voice command (e.g., "create a test markdown file in my skills repo") and automatically generate a GitHub pull request in the background.
  • Evaluating GPT-5.5 via Snapcat: A historical benchmark.
    • Matias uses "Snapcat" (an iPad app developed at a 24-hour hackathon 10 years ago that uses a moving laser dot to capture front-facing cat photos) to test new model iterations.
    • With GPT-5.5, the model successfully "one-shotted" the app skeleton and rebuilt complex UI setting screens using generative design prompts.
  • Computer Use Automation: Offloading tedious administrative tasks.
    • Matias used Anthropic's computer use feature to SSH into a Raspberry Pi and copy-paste domain URLs into an admin panel, completing the task completely hands-free.

Notable Quotes

"We are very much assuming that 100% of developers are building software with the help of AI... The developer we're building for has evolved." — *Matias Castello*
"I can prompt Codex before going to bed to go do some research about an app that I have, tell it to build the top 10 features... and wake up to 10 feature flags that I can toggle on and off." — *Matias Castello*
"If you have an idea, more often than not, it can probably be done... Assume you can do it. In this case, maybe be in denial even that you can do it." — *Matias Castello*
"When you try to get something out of an LLM and it doesn't work, you have to put your ego aside and assume it's your fault. Don't assume the tool isn't capable, assume you haven't found a way to communicate or convey what you want just yet." — *Matias Castello*
Tu es prêt ? On commence ? C'est parti. Matias, thank you for joining. Thank you for having me. Really happy to be here. I'm really excited to chat because you have a very unique background. You've crossed a bunch of worlds. You worked in consumer products, you worked on developer platforms like at Facebook in the early days, and now leading product for Alchemy in the crypto space. But what I find even more interesting is that you're not an engineer by training, and yet you're building more than many engineers that I know. How do you go about it? Nvidia’s Jensen Huang on the AI revolution, job losses and what drives him | Full interview

CNA(3.2M) ·56:13 ·25.0K views · 2026-05-29
Jensen Huang (Founder and CEO, Nvidia)
Nvidia founder and CEO Jensen Huang outlines an optimistic future for the AI revolution, rejecting lazy narratives of widespread job loss and detailing how AI will expand global GDP, elevate human ambition, and inject trillions into technology and manufacturing supply chains.
TL;DR Nvidia founder and CEO Jensen Huang outlines an optimistic future for the AI revolution, rejecting lazy narratives of widespread job loss and detailing how AI will expand global GDP, elevate human ambition, and inject trillions into technology and manufacturing supply...

TL;DR

Nvidia founder and CEO Jensen Huang outlines an optimistic future for the AI revolution, rejecting lazy narratives of widespread job loss and detailing how AI will expand global GDP, elevate human ambition, and inject trillions into technology and manufacturing supply chains.

The "5-Layer Cake" of AI and the Rise of Agentic AI

  • The 5-Layer AI Framework: Huang conceptualizes the AI industry not merely as software models, but as a holistic, five-layer stack that is reinventing every major industry:
      • *Layer 1 (Energy):* The foundational base. AI is generated in real-time and requires immense physical power grids.
      • *Layer 2 (Chips):* The hardware layer where Nvidia and its global partners operate.
      • *Layer 3 (Infrastructure):* The land, data centers, and cloud software that turn silicon into cloud service.
      • *Layer 4 (Models):* Systems that process multi-modal data—not just language, but videos, proteins, chemicals, and 3D geometries for manufacturing.
      • *Layer 5 (Applications):* The end-user software revolutionizing information work, healthcare, self-driving cars, and robotics.
  • Agentic AI: This refers to autonomous AI pipelines that have "agency" to execute tasks with minimal human supervision.
      • *The Workflow:* These agents understand context, plan their work, select and deploy digital tools (such as word processors, browsers, or Python compilers), and continuously self-evaluate and iterate until a goal is met.
      • *Physical Representation:* Agentic AI exists both digitally (as software assistants) and physically (as autonomous robots).

Debunking the AI Job Loss Narrative

  • The "Lazy" Executive Narrative: Huang strongly criticizes corporate leaders who blame AI for recent layoffs, calling it a "lazy" excuse to sound smart.
      • *Timing Inconsistency:* He notes that AI only became highly productive in the last six months, making it historically impossible to blame it for workforce reductions occurring over the last two years.
  • The Ambition Multiplier: Historically, automation technology (PCs, the internet, mobile cloud) has never made humans less busy. Instead, it elevates human ambition, allowing society to tackle much larger, more complex problems.
      • *Task vs. Purpose:* Jobs are "baskets of tasks." While AI will automate specific *tasks*, it will not eliminate the *purpose* of the job (e.g., a radiologist's purpose is diagnosing disease; automating image scanning allows them to focus on high-value patient care).
  • The Golden Rule of AI Employment: "You're not going to lose your job to AI; you're going to lose your job to someone who learned AI better than you." Huang urges parents and youth to engage with and master the technology rather than reject it.
  • Job Creation Across the Stack: Massive employment is being generated at every layer of the AI infrastructure:
      • *Energy & Infrastructure:* Major investment is surging into power grid upgrades, sustainable energy, and data center construction, employing hundreds of thousands of electricians, plumbers, and architects.
      • *Venture Capital:* A historic $100 billion was funneled into AI-native startups in a single year.
      • *Radiology Case Study:* Despite predictions a decade ago that radiology would be wiped out by AI, the demand, pay, and total head count of radiologists have all increased.

Geopolitics: US-China Dynamics and Taiwan's Central Role

  • China as a Formidable Competitor: China remains a massive rival in tech due to its large, uniform local market, a highly educated population, top-tier academic institutions (like Tsinghua University), and deeply vibrant tech giants (Alibaba, Xiaomi, Tencent, Baidu).
      • *Sanctions Backfire:* US export controls left a market vacuum in China, enabling domestic companies like Huawei to achieve record growth.
      • *Cooperation vs. Separation:* Huang argues that a total split into two separate AI ecosystems is unwise. While the US and China will compete, they must cooperate on safety, guardrails, and regulatory standards.
  • Taiwan at the Center of the AI Universe: Taiwan remains the absolute epicenter of the physical AI supply chain.
      • *The $1 Trillion Pipeline:* Across Nvidia's upcoming Grace Blackwell and Vera Rubin architectures, Nvidia projects $1 trillion in sales, which will channel hundreds of billions of dollars of revenue directly into Taiwanese manufacturing and packaging partners.
      • *Resilience & Growth:* Global supply chains are diversifying and building fabs worldwide, but Taiwan’s local industry continues to expand at an outpaced, accelerated rate.
      • *Morris Chang Partnership:* Huang highlights his deep personal and professional relationship with the TSMC founder, noting that Nvidia simply would not exist without TSMC's early risk-taking and support.

Jensen Huang’s Leadership Style and Nvidia’s Succession

  • The "Taiwanese Parent" Management Style: Huang famously prefers to "torture employees to greatness" rather than fire them.
      • *The Methodology:* He describes his style as incredibly demanding, providing immediate, direct criticism because he knows his team can do better—but immediately returning to a supportive, mentoring stance once the feedback is delivered.
      • *Retention Rate:* Despite this intense culture, Nvidia maintains some of the highest employee retention rates in the tech world, with some staff members staying for over 33 years.
  • Personal Drive and Work Ethic: Huang works seven days a week, driven by a deep fear of failure, the burden of supporting a massive global ecosystem of partners, and an ambitious desire to see his "dreamer" visions realized in his lifetime. He states he hopes to "die on the job."
  • The Next Generation of Leadership: The eventual successor to Nvidia is already working inside the company.
      • *Changing Leadership Criteria:* As technical skills, coding, and problem-solving become automated commodities, future leaders must possess exceptional "soft skills." Huang believes the ultimate asset of a future leader will be their character, empathy, selflessness, and the desire of everyone around them to see them succeed.

Why Two IIT Engineers Turned Down $550K Jobs To Build A Startup

Y Combinator(2.3M) ·24:30 ·9.8K views · 2026-05-29
Varun Vummadi (Co-founder, Giga) Ankit Gupta (General Partner, Y Combinator)
Varun Vummadi turned down a $550,000 quant finance offer and a Stanford PhD to build GigaML, eventually leveraging Y Combinator's network and a lean 8-person team to secure major enterprise clients like DoorDash over well-funded, 400-person competitors.
TL;DR Varun Vummadi turned down a $550,000 quant finance offer and a Stanford PhD to build GigaML, eventually leveraging Y Combinator's network and a lean 8-person team to secure major enterprise clients like DoorDash over well-funded, 400-person competitors. Rejecting Elite...

TL;DR

Varun Vummadi turned down a $550,000 quant finance offer and a Stanford PhD to build GigaML, eventually leveraging Y Combinator's network and a lean 8-person team to secure major enterprise clients like DoorDash over well-funded, 400-person competitors.

The Non-Linear Path to Product-Market Fit

  • Rejecting Elite Safety Nets: Driven by the launch of ChatGPT, Varun Vummadi and his co-founder turned down highly lucrative opportunities—including a $550,000 New York City quant trading offer and a Stanford PhD program—just three days before they were set to begin.
  • The YC Pivots:
      • The founders originally entered Y Combinator with an LLM-based ed-tech idea.
      • During the interview, YC Partner Harj Taggar told them the ed-tech market was unviable but accepted them anyway due to their strong engineering backgrounds.
      • After briefly pivoting to an LLM fine-tuning and caching service (which topped Hugging Face benchmarks and raised a $4 million seed round), they noticed their only growing customer use cases were coding and customer support.
      • This insight led them to pivot fully into AI-driven customer support, signing Zepto as their first major customer.

Defeating Giants: How a Lean Team Won DoorDash

  • Beating a 400-Person Competitor: Operating as a lean team of just eight people, GigaML went head-to-head with a massive, heavily funded incumbent competitor to win DoorDash's enterprise customer service contract.
  • The YC Network Multiplier: To get his foot in the door, YC President Garry Tan introduced Varun directly to DoorDash CEO Tony Xu. Because both startups were YC alumni, an inherent layer of trust allowed GigaML to bypass traditional enterprise sales friction and secure a three-month pilot.
  • Superior Deflection Metrics:
      • Traditional customer support IVR and chatbots yield a 10% to 15% deflection rate.
      • GigaML's conversational AI agents achieve a 60% to 70% deflection rate, with target goals of 90% to 95% for top-tier enterprise clients.
      • The core of their technical edge relies on "iterating markdown policy files" to consistently move customer KPIs like CSAT and resolution rates.

Driving Hyper-Leverage via Internal AI Automation

  • A 7x Engineering Force Multiplier: GigaML keeps its internal headcount incredibly low by heavily utilizing coding agents. Varun estimates that without tools like Claude, GigaML would require six to seven times more engineers to maintain their current shipping velocity.
  • "Vibe Coding" Interview Tactics: GigaML tests job candidates by allowing them to "vibe code" alongside AI assistants during the interview. To ensure deep technical understanding, they then strip away the AI tools and ask candidates to manually debug and modify the generated codebase.
  • Enterprise AI Deployments: Varun identifies the traditional "forward deployed engineer" as the primary bottleneck in enterprise AI adoption. GigaML is currently building an autonomous "AI forward deployed engineer" designed to join Slack channels and Google Meets, synthesize notes, and automatically deploy system changes.

Hard-Earned Advice for College Founders

  • Burn the Boats: Varun attributes their survival to the psychological pressure of rejecting their high-paying job offers. Having no fallback plan forced them to make the business work.
  • Charge Customers Early: Startups should avoid offering free pilots for too long. If a business problem is painful enough, a customer will pay real money or time for it. If they refuse to pay, the founder is solving a "fake problem."
  • Product Over Sales: In the generative AI era, product quality dictates success. Top AI companies like OpenAI and Anthropic scale rapidly due to value-delivery, not aggressive sales commission structures.

Notable Quotes

"We're like eight people going against this 400-person well-funded company and we won... That's when we truly realized that there is a lot of arbitrage of actually building a great product rather than a sales team." — Varun Vummadi
"It actually forces you to make things... Just like going at it and doing things has a lot stronger value. Especially with AI, because the cost of building things is so low, people should just build things and try to deliver as much value as they can to a very small set of customers and see if they can pay them money." — Varun Vummadi
"If the problem is important enough, people should be willing to pay money for it or else you're just solving a fake problem." — Varun Vummadi
